Mark Lizaola< /name>
<Date>1606332873335< /Date><rating>1<//rating>< text>
Clearly Nichol's Lumber motive is profit.  Which is unfortunate because I have made the switch from a big box store to shop local and ended up getting ripped off for unusable materials.

Worked with the purchasing manager Rick Deen who guaranteed me a solution in person for there brittle/flaking birch and then ghosted me.  I ended up having to go in person and he told me in the most condescending manner that it was me and not that and that he owes me nothing.

(We do custom fabrications on the daily for some of the biggest musicians in the game and directly for the largest music festivals in the country - with out a doubt there's no issue with our experience or equipment)

This is what's wrong with small Business these days is they forget they are also the little guy and that us small players become there large contracts.

If you're looking for a place to pick up lumber that respects and values it's customers I can assure you this is not the place.

This place is not worth the hassle that comes along with it.< /text>

<Review>Bottom line, these gentlemen are top notch!  I so appreciate their quick response, punctuality, easy to understand communication, thoroughness of plan, a fair estimate, attention to detail, and the work done to perfection.  I will not hesitate to call them for future projects.

Here's my story. After looking for two years and against my better judgement I bought a flipped house.  The home inspection was clean for a 60 year old house, but of course the house has since revealed more problems than I had been led to believe.

Last winter after heavy rains, I noticed some discoloration and dampness on a small section of baseboard.  No major wetness, but something wasn't right.  During the summer I decided to get some bids before winter returned.  Two companies came out, but the solutions they proposed didn't make sense to me and on top of that, both were late for the appointment, one by four hours. Neither one suggested taking off the baseboard to see what may be happening behind it.

Then Alex from Cobex came out.  He was on time, personable and quickly pinpointed what was most likely the source of the problem and explained it in a way that made sense to me.  From there he scheduled an appointment to have one of his experienced associates come out to take off the interior baseboard and to peek behind the exterior siding. He corroborated what Alex suspected was shoddy installation of two new windows and a new slider by the previous owner.  The same afternoon, Alex came out and really spent time discussing a solution and a very detailed plan of action that was easy for me to visualize.  The following morning I received an email from Alex that thoroughly depicted the plan including proposal, materials and timeframe, from start to finish and even included possible contingency plans, in case when further into the walls, the damage was more than anticipated, along with what I thought was a fair estimate for a lot of work that included pulling up and re-stretching carpet, mold remediation, removing and reinstalling base board and exterior siding and trim, sealing badly installed windows and slider, caulking and painting inside and out.

Alex quickly fit me in to his busy schedule and was sensitive that winter was fast approaching and wanted to get the work done for me before the wet season returned. His workers were friendly, respectful, trustworthy, showed up on time and did exactly what I expected and cleaned up beautifully.  Everything looked flawless, neat and tidy and completed on time. After they left, Alex came out to inspect the work.  He found a few slight imperfections, that I didn't even notice, and had someone come out the following day for a touch up. Just wonderful!</Review>< name>

<Review>My wife and I contracted with Cobex Construction Group to make improvements, upgrades and repairs to our home in the Ridgewiew Neighborhood El Dorado Hills.  The house is a one of one design by the architect owner that we have owned for 4 years.

My review will be in several parts because  the projects will take time during the winter months.  I can't say enough good things about their estimating and contracting process, workmanship and follow up on all aspects of the work.

From the beginning, getting an initial estimate and many discussions about what would look best  from design through construction was informative and excellent.  Everything was covered, no guess work and full disclosure if there were issues spotted and how we wanted to proceed.

The project consisted of updating the kitchen with new Quartzite surfaces and some appliances.  The Quartzite is a natural stone from Brazil and the backslash is glass subway tile that we purchased from Bedrosians.  We had the electrical switches and plugs updated with Legrand Adorna.  A new Sharp drawer microwave, Bosch dishwasher and a GE Profile cook top hood. The microwave required cabinet modifications and the hood required cutting the stone surround to fit the vent which it was done perfectly.  The cabinet modifications were completed with precision and even the touch up paint for the farm house cabinets matched perfectly.

Our kitchen had solid granite counter tops that were installed when the house was new, 2001.  The counter tops had seams in the granite that went through the sinks and were not level or really match up.

The COBEX crew came in an put down heavy duty paper to protect our Hickory floors. They put up a sheet plastic wall around the kitchen to keep the dust from going into the dining area and family room.  They removed all of the granite counter tops, the island and back splash behind the cook top.

Afterward, everything was spotlessly vacuumed up and taken away.  Next they put down new plywood counter top base and backer board for the tile back splash, nearly 70 SQ feet.  They made all of their templates and off to the fabricator.

The fabricator returned and removed more of the stone surround for the cook top and one wall cabinet.  He had fabricated the counters all, without any seams.  He and his crew worked tirelessly to fit these huge pieces in perfectly.  FYI.  The quartzite is a very hard natural stone and it took extra time to cut and shape.  The tile setter did an amazing job with the glass subway tile and moving the electrical boxes to a high level on the wall.  It sparkles and looks fantastic.

We stood in the kitchen just admiring the stone and the craftsmanship.  We had a party two weeks ago and everyone was impressed with the kitchen and their amazing craftsmanship.

We had all of the rain gutters replaced as the old one were in poor shape.  The COBEX construction group had the sub contractor measure everything and consulted me all along the way.  After the gutters were installed, Alex from COBEX walked the entire perimeter with the gutter fabricator to insure everything was perfect.

We also had the eaves inspected for dry rot, the COBEX crew came though, stripped back 2 rows of tile, removed the damaged areas and replaced everything very nicely.  Alex walked the entire roof with the sub-contractor to follow up on all of the repairs and to insure everything was perfect.

Last will be the upgrade of the 2 HVAC units in a very tight a difficult area.

I'll be writing as these next projects get completed.  With the rainy weather it will take a little longer.

Alex, Vaz and the COBEX team are fantastic and respond to every email or question we have had.< /Review><pictures>None< /pictures>< Response>
